ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-item {
    counter-increment: list-counter-alpha;
}

ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-marker::before {
    content: counter(list-counter-alpha, lower-alpha);
}

/* Level 3: Lowercase roman numerals */

    counter-reset: list-counter-roman;
}

    counter-increment: list-counter-roman;
}

ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-marker::before {
    content: counter(list-counter-roman, lower-roman);
}

<p>At the end of the cycle, the students should be able to:</p>
<ol>
<li>Identify the nurse's roles in the prevention of cancer and in health education.</li>
<li>Discuss the pathophysiology of cancer and its clinical manifestations.</li>
<li>Apply the nursing process to identify care of the client in the diagnosis and treatment phases of cancer.</li>
<li>Formulate plan of care for the client with early stage and advanced cancer.</li>
<li>Value the nurse's role in providing quality, comprehensive, individualized, ethical and humane care of clients with cancer.</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="orientation-of-the-course">Orientation of the Course<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#orientation-of-the-course" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="basic-concepts">Basic Concepts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#basic-concepts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>01</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-6a89d0df.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-c4b00a67.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="terminologies">Terminologies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#terminologies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>CANCER</th><th>a disease of the cell in which the normal mechanisms of the control of growth and proliferation have been altered</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>MALIGNANT NEOPLASM</td><td>it is invasive, spreading directly to surrounding tissues as well as to new sites in the body</td></tr><tr><td>BENIGN NEOPLASM</td><td>a harmless growth that does not spread or invade other tissues</td></tr><tr><td>NEOPLASIA</td><td>abnormal cellular changes and growth of new tissues</td></tr><tr><td>HYPERPLASIA</td><td>increase in cell number</td></tr><tr><td>HYPERTROPHY</td><td>increase in cell size</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="terminologies">Terminologies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#terminologies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>METAPLASIA</th><th>replacement of one adult cell type by a different adult cell type</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>DYSPLASIA</td><td>changes in cell size, shape, organization</td></tr><tr><td>ANAPLASIA</td><td>reverse cellular development to a more primitive or embryonic cell type</td></tr><tr><td>METASTASES</td><td>spread of cancer cells to distant parts of the body to set up new tumors</td></tr><tr><td>ONCOLOGY</td><td>the medical specialty that deals with diagnosis, treatment, and study of cancer</td></tr><tr><td>CARCINOGENS</td><td>factors associated with cancer causation</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-cancer">Types of Cancer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-cancer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>01</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adenocarcinoma">Adenocarcinoma<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adenocarcinoma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>cancer that arises from glandular tissues (breast, lung, thyroid, colon and pancreas CA)</p>
<p>02</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="carcinoma">Carcinoma<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#carcinoma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>cancer that is composed of epithelial cells; develops in tissues covering or lining organs of the body such as skin, uterus or breast</p>
<p>03</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sarcoma">Sarcoma<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sarcoma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>cancer of supporting or connecting tissues such as cartilage, bones, muscles or fats</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-0754a9fa.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathogenesis-of-cancer">Pathogenesis of Cancer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathogenesis-of-cancer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>01</p>
<p>Cellular Transformation and Derangement Theory</p>
<p>normal cells may be transformed into cancer cells due to exposure to some etiologic agents</p>
<p>02</p>
<p>Failure of the Immune Response Theory</p>
<p>all individuals possess cancer cells, however, recognized by the immune response system</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-0839257c.jpeg" alt="img-5.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="etiologic-factors">Etiologic Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiologic-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-7b3ad6a8.jpeg" alt="img-6.jpeg"> Viruses</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-adcf934e.jpeg" alt="img-7.jpeg"> Chemical carcinogens</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-27cfa5e8.jpeg" alt="img-8.jpeg"> Physical agents</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-3541560a.jpeg" alt="img-9.jpeg"> Hormones</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-67533f0e.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg"> Genetics</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-6ae3d231.jpeg" alt="img-11.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-4459da64.jpeg" alt="img-12.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="viruses-and-bacteria">VIRUSES and BACTERIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#viruses-and-bacteria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-fef5747f.jpeg" alt="img-13.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>oncogenic viruses may be one of the multiple agents acting to initiate carcinogenesis</li>
<li>prolonged or frequent viral infections may cause breakdown of the immune system or overwhelm the immune system</li>
<li>infections that increase risk of certain forms of cancer are as follows:
&gt; Human Papilloma Virus (HPV)  cervical cancer
&gt; Epstein-Barr Virus  lymphoma
&gt; Hepatitis B and C  hepatocellular cancer
&gt; Helicobacter Pylori  gastric cancer</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-359dd685.jpeg" alt="img-14.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chemical-carcinogens">CHEMICAL CARCINOGENS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-carcinogens" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-1bfece4c.jpeg" alt="img-15.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>causing cell mutation or alteration in cell enzymes and proteins causing altered cell replication</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>INDUSTRIAL COMPOUNDS</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>vinyl chloride (used for plastic manufacture, asbestos factories, construction works)</li>
<li>polycyclic aromatic hydrocarbons (such as from refuse burning, auto and truck emissions, oil refineries, air pollution)</li>
<li>fertilizers, weed killers</li>
<li>dyes (aniline dyes used in beauty shops, hair bleach)</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-7830b5e8.jpeg" alt="img-16.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chemical-carcinogens">CHEMICAL CARCINOGENS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-carcinogens" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-59d05ac2.jpeg" alt="img-17.jpeg"></p>
<ol start="2">
<li>DRUGS</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>tobacco (tar nicotine), 90% of all cases of lung CA are due to smoking</li>
<li>alcohol</li>
<li>cytotoxic drugs</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>HORMONES</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>diethylstilbestrol (DES)  non-steroidal estrogen medication used for pregnancy support, hormone therapy for menopausal symptoms and estrogen deficiency</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>FOODS, PRESERVATIVES</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>nitrates (bacon, smoked meat)</li>
<li>talc (polished rice, salami, chewing gum)</li>
<li>food sweeteners</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chemical-carcinogens">CHEMICAL CARCINOGENS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-carcinogens" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-e859d520.jpeg" alt="img-18.jpeg"></p>
<ol start="4">
<li>FOODS, PRESERVATIVES</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>nitrates (bacon, smoked meat)</li>
<li>talc (polished rice, salami, chewing gum)</li>
<li>food sweeteners</li>
<li>nitrosamines (rubber baby nipples)</li>
<li>aflatoxins (mold in nuts and grains, milk, cheese, peanut butter)</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>POLYCYCLIC HYDROCARBON</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>charcoal broiling</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-efb8d781.jpeg" alt="img-19.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-e731c99d.jpeg" alt="img-20.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="physical-agents">PHYSICAL AGENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physical-agents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>RADIATION</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>from X-rays or radioactive isotopes</li>
<li>from sunlight/UV rays</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>PHYSICAL IRRITATION/TRAUMA</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>from pipe smoking</li>
<li>multiple deliveries</li>
<li>jagged tooth</li>
<li>irritation of the tongue</li>
<li>overuse of any organ/body part</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-2ec76008.jpeg" alt="img-21.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hormones">HORMONES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hormones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-b58a2dc5.jpeg" alt="img-22.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>estrogen as replacement therapy has been found to increase incidence of vaginal, cervical and uterine CAs</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-e0eb9875.jpeg" alt="img-23.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="genetics">GENETICS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#genetics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>when oncogene (hidden or repressed genetic code for cancer that exists in all individuals) is exposed to carcinogens, changes in cell structure occurs, malignant tumor develops</li>
<li>regardless of the cause, several cancers are associated with familial patterns</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-e0eb9875.jpeg" alt="img-24.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="predisposing-factors">Predisposing Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>|  AGE | - older individuals are more prone to cancer because they have been exposed to carcinogens longer</p>
<ul>
<li>they have developed alterations in the immune system  |
| --- | --- |
|  SEX | - the most common type of cancer in females is breast cancer, and prostate cancer in males  |
|  URBAN vs RURAL RESIDENCE | - cancer is more common among urban dwellers than among rural residents, probably due to greater exposure to carcinogens, more stressful lifestyle and greater consumption of preservatives  |</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="predisposing-factors">Predisposing Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>|  GEOGRAPHIC DISTRIBUTION | - most common type of cancer in Japan is gastric cancer, in USA is breast cancer</p>
<ul>
<li>may be due to influence of environmental factors such diet (raw foods greatly consist Japanese diet), ethnic customs, types of pollution  |
| --- | --- |
|  OCCUPATION | - there is greater risk of exposure to carcinogens among chemical factory workers, farmers, radiology department personnel  |
|  HEREDITY | - positive family history of cancer increases risk to develop the disease in adults, approximately (34% of cancers have a familial basis)  |</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="predisposing-factors">Predisposing Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>|  STRESS | - depression, grief, anger, aggression, despair, or life stresses <strong>decrease immunocompetence</strong> because of affectation of hypothalamus and pituitary gland</p>
<ul>
<li>immunodeficiency may spur the growth and proliferation of cancer cells  |
| --- | --- |
|  PRECANCEROUS LESIONS | - pigmented moles, burn scars, senile keratosis, leukopenia, benign polyps or adenoma of the colon or stomach, fibrocystic dse. of the breast, may undergo transformation into cancerous lesions and tumors  |
|  OBESITY | - studies have linked obesity to breast and colorectal cancer  |</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="characteristics-of-benign-and-malignant-neoplasm">Characteristics of Benign and Malignant Neoplasm<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-benign-and-malignant-neoplasm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>BENIGN</th><th>MALIGNANT</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>grows slowly</td><td>grows rapidly</td></tr><tr><td>remains localized</td><td>infiltrates surrounding tissues</td></tr><tr><td>encapsulated</td><td>not encapsulated</td></tr><tr><td>well-differentiated mature cells, but cells poorly function</td><td>poorly-differentiated; anaplastic/embryonic type of cells</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-1fe5c5ce.jpeg" alt="img-25.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-873ea244.jpeg" alt="img-26.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="characteristics-of-benign-and-malignant-neoplasm">Characteristics of Benign and Malignant Neoplasm<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-benign-and-malignant-neoplasm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>BENIGN</th><th>MALIGNANT</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>extremely unusual when surgically removed</td><td>commonly following surgery because of spread to other tissues</td></tr><tr><td>never occur</td><td>very common</td></tr><tr><td>not harmful to host, unless it compresses tissues or obstruct vital organ</td><td>always harmful to host, may result in necrosis, ulcerations, hemorrhage, infection</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-411e1c69.jpeg" alt="img-27.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-fa99b1bf.jpeg" alt="img-28.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="characteristics-of-benign-and-malignant-neoplasm">Characteristics of Benign and Malignant Neoplasm<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-benign-and-malignant-neoplasm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-24bdf802.jpeg" alt="img-29.jpeg"></p>
<p>Prognosis</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>BENIGN</th><th>MALIGNANT</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>very good</td><td>poor prognosis if cells are poorly differentiated and evidence of metastasis</td></tr></tbody></table>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-screening-and-early-detection">Prevention, Screening and Early Detection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-screening-and-early-detection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-f2991c92.jpeg" alt="img-34.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention">Prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="primary-prevention">PRIMARY PREVENTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>activities are aimed at prevention before pathologic change has begun</li>
<li>can help reduce cancer risk through alteration of lifestyle behaviors to eliminate or reduce exposure to carcinogens</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; adapting more healthy diet
&gt; limiting exposure to sun and other sources of UV radiation
&gt; modifying sexual practices
&gt; avoiding cigarettes smoking and alcohol drinking
&gt; decreasing exposure to environmental and occupational carcinogens</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="seconary-prevention">SECONARY PREVENTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#seconary-prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>early detection, provides the opportunity to detect precancerous lesions or early-stage cancers, to treat them promptly</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="early-detection">Early Detection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#early-detection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>American Cancer Society (ACS) Recommendations for the Early Detection of Cancer in Asymptomatic People</p>
<ul>
<li>cancer-related check-up:</li>
</ul>
<table><thead><tr><th>AGE</th><th>FREQUENCY</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>20 to 40 years</td><td>every 3 years</td></tr><tr><td>40 years and older</td><td>annual</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>02</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>AGE</th><th>BREAST EXAMINATIONS and FREQUENCY</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>20 to 39 years</td><td>- have clinical breast exam (CBE) every 3 years</td></tr></tbody></table>
<ul>
<li>perform breast self-exam (BSE) monthly  |
|  40 years and older | - annual mammogram</li>
<li>annual CBE</li>
<li>perform breast self-exam (BSE) monthly  |</li>
</ul>
<p>03</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>AGE</th><th>COLON AND RECTUM EXAMINATIONS and FREQUENCY</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>50 years and older (men/women)</td><td>- annual fecal occult blood tests</td></tr></tbody></table>
<ul>
<li>flexible sigmoidoscopy every 5 years</li>
<li>colonoscopy every 10 years</li>
<li>double-contrast barium enema every 5 -10 years</li>
<li>digital rectal exam (DRE) done at the same time as sigmoidoscopy, colonoscopy or double-contrast barium enema  |</li>
</ul>
<p>04</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>AGE</th><th>PROSTATE EXAMINATIONS and FREQUENCY</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>50 years and older</td><td>- <strong>annual</strong> prostate-specific antigen (PSA) blood test</td></tr></tbody></table>
<ul>
<li><strong>annual</strong> DRE  |</li>
</ul>
<p>05</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>PROFILE</th><th>UTERINE EXAMINATIONS and FREQUENCY</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>women who are or have been sexually active</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>or 40 years and older</td><td>CERVIX</td></tr></tbody></table>
<ul>
<li><strong>annual</strong> Pap smear test and pelvic exam (after 3 or more consecutive satisfactory exams with normal findings, may be performed less frequently)</li>
<li>HPV test is recommended  |
|  started menopause | ENDOMETRIUM</li>
<li>endometrial biopsy  |</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dietary-recommendations">Dietary Recommendations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dietary-recommendations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>American Cancer Society (ACS) Recommendations Against Cancer</p>
<ol>
<li>Avoid obesity</li>
<li>Cut down on total fat intake</li>
<li>Eat more high fiber foods, like raw fruits and vegetables, whole grain cereals</li>
<li>Include foods rich in vit A and C in daily diet</li>
<li>Include cruciferous vegetables in the diet like broccoli, cabbage, cauliflower, Brussel sprouts</li>
<li>Be moderate in the consumption of alcoholic beverages</li>
<li>Be moderate in the consumption of salt-cured, smoked-cured and nitrate-cured foods</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="common-causes-of-cancer">Common Causes of Cancer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-causes-of-cancer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>|  BREAST CANCER | - early menarche</p>
<ul>
<li>late menopause</li>
<li>nulliparous or older than 30 years at the birth of a first child  |
| --- | --- |
|  LUNG CANCER | - tobacco abuse</li>
<li>asbestos</li>
<li>radiation exposure</li>
<li>air pollution  |
|  COLORECTAL CANCER | - greater incidence in men</li>
<li>familial polyposis</li>
<li>ulcerative colitis</li>
<li>high-fat, low-fiber diet  |</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="common-causes-of-cancer">Common Causes of Cancer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-causes-of-cancer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>|  PROSTATE CANCER | - common among males who are 50 years and older</p>
<ul>
<li>African-American have the highest incidence in the world</li>
<li>(+) family history</li>
<li>exposure to cadmium  |
| --- | --- |
|  CERVICAL CANCER | - sexual behavior:</li>
</ul>
<blockquote>
<p>first intercourse at an early age
multiple sexual partners
sexual partner who has had multiple sexual partners</p>
</blockquote>
<ul>
<li>(+) HPV and AIDS</li>
<li>low socioeconomic status</li>
<li>cigarette smoking  |</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="common-causes-of-cancer">Common Causes of Cancer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-causes-of-cancer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>|  HEAD AND NECK CANCER | - more common among males</p>
<ul>
<li>alcohol and tobacco use</li>
<li>poor oral hygiene</li>
<li>long term sun exposure</li>
<li>occupational  |
| --- | --- |
|  SKIN CANCER | - individuals with fair complexion</li>
<li>(+) family history</li>
<li>moles (nevi)</li>
<li>exposure to coal tar, creosote, arsenic, radium</li>
<li>sun exposure between 11am to 3pm  |</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="warning-signals-of-cancer">Warning Signals of Cancer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#warning-signals-of-cancer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>C</th><th>change in bowel or bladder habits</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>A</td><td>a sore that does not heal</td></tr><tr><td>U</td><td>unusual bleeding or discharge</td></tr><tr><td>U</td><td>unexplained anemia</td></tr><tr><td>U</td><td>unexplained sudden weight loss</td></tr><tr><td>T</td><td>thickening or lump in the breast or elsewhere</td></tr><tr><td>I</td><td>Indigestion or difficulty swallowing</td></tr><tr><td>O</td><td>obvious change in wart or mole</td></tr><tr><td>N</td><td>nagging cough or hoarseness of voice</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="staging-and-grading-of-neoplasia">Staging and Grading of Neoplasia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staging-and-grading-of-neoplasia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="staging">STAGING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staging" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>determining the size of the tumor and existence of metastases</li>
<li>necessary at the time of diagnosis to determine:
&gt; extent of disease (local vs metastatic);
&gt; prognosis
&gt; proper management</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="grading">GRADING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#grading" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>classification of tumor cells</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="staging-and-grading-of-neoplasia">Staging and Grading of Neoplasia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staging-and-grading-of-neoplasia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Stage</th><th>What it means</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Stage 0</td><td>Abnormal cells are present but have not spread to nearby tissue. Also called carcinoma in situ, or CIS. CIS is not cancer, but it may become cancer.</td></tr><tr><td>Stage I, Stage II, and Stage III (may also be written as Stage 1, Stage 2, and Stage 3)</td><td>Cancer is present. The higher the number, the larger the cancer tumor and the more it has spread into nearby tissues.</td></tr><tr><td>Stage IV (may also be written as Stage 4)</td><td>The cancer has spread to distant parts of the body.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="staging-and-grading-of-neoplasia">Staging and Grading of Neoplasia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staging-and-grading-of-neoplasia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>NOMENCLATURE OF NEOPLASIA</p>
<ul>
<li>tumor is named according to:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>
<p>PARENCHYMA
Hepatoma- liver
Osteoma- bone
Myoma- muscle</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>PATTERN AND STRUCTURE, either gross or microscopic
Fluid-filled- Cyst
Glandular- Adeno
Finger-like- Papillo
Stalk- Polyp</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>EMBRYONIC ORIGIN
Ectoderm- usually gives rise to epithelium
Endoderm- glands
Mesoderm- connective tissues</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="staging-and-grading-of-neoplasia">Staging and Grading of Neoplasia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staging-and-grading-of-neoplasia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>BENIGN TUMOR</th><th>MALIGNANT TUMOR</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>- suffix used, -OMA</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>adipose tissue- LipOMA</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>bone- osteOMA</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>muscle- myOMA</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>blood vessels- angiOMA</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>fibrous tissue- fibrOMA</td><td>1. Ectodermal, endodermal, glandular, epithelial</td></tr></tbody></table>
<ul>
<li>suffix used, -CARCINOMA
Pancreatic AdenoCARCINOMA
Squamous Cell CARCINOMA</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Mesodermal, connective tissue origin</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>suffix used, -SARCOMA
FibroSARCOMA
MyoSARCOMA
AngioSARCOMA  |</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="staging-and-grading-of-neoplasia">Staging and Grading of Neoplasia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staging-and-grading-of-neoplasia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>-OMA but Malignant
HepatOMA, LymphOMA, GliOMA, MelanOMA</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>THREE-germ layers, -TERATOMA</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Non-neoplastic but -OMA
HematOMA</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tnm-classification">TNM Classification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tnm-classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>a system developed by American Joint Committee of Cancer (AJCC) that can be applied to all tumor types</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="t-primary-main-tumor-size">T - primary/main tumor size<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#t-primary-main-tumor-size" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Tx  primary tumor is unable to be assessed
To  no evidence of primary tumor
T1s  carcinoma in situ (abnormal cells are present but have not spread to nearby tissue)
T1, T2, T3, T4  increasing size and/or local extent of primary tumor</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="n-presence-or-absence-of-regional-nearby-lymph-node-involvement">N - presence or absence of regional nearby lymph node involvement<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#n-presence-or-absence-of-regional-nearby-lymph-node-involvement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Nx  regional lymph nodes are unable to be assessed
No  no regional lymph nodes involvement
N1, N2, N3  increasing involvement of regional lymph nodes</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="m-presence-or-absence-of-distant-metastases">M - presence or absence of distant metastases<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#m-presence-or-absence-of-distant-metastases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Mx  unable to be assessed
Mo  absence of distant metastases
M1  presence of distant metastases</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="identifying-information">Identifying information<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#identifying-information" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="venus">Venus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#venus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cancer-detection-examinations">Cancer Detection Examinations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cancer-detection-examinations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cytologic-examination-or-papanicolaou-test-pap-s-exam-pap-smear">CYTOLOGIC EXAMINATION OR PAPANICOLAOU TEST (PAP'S EXAM, PAP SMEAR)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cytologic-examination-or-papanicolaou-test-pap-s-exam-pap-smear" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>cytologic specimen can be obtained from tumors that tend to shed cells from their surface</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; GI tract through endoscopy
&gt; GU tract through colposcopy of the cervix and vagina
&gt; cystoscopy of the bladder
&gt; laparoscopy of the pelvic and abdominal cavity</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-e5afff94.jpeg" alt="img-40.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cancer-detection-examinations">Cancer Detection Examinations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cancer-detection-examinations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cytologic-examination-or-papanicolaou-test-pap-s-exam-pap-smear">CYTOLOGIC EXAMINATION OR PAPANICOLAOU TEST (PAP'S EXAM, PAP SMEAR)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cytologic-examination-or-papanicolaou-test-pap-s-exam-pap-smear" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>interpretation of Papanicolaou Test results are as follows:</li>
</ul>
<table><thead><tr><th>Class I</th><th>Normal</th><th>follow-up examination every 1-3 yrs as recommended by physician</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Class II</td><td>Inflammation</td><td>may require Pap exam in 3-6 mos as prescribed</td></tr><tr><td>Class III</td><td>Mild to moderate dysplasia</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Class IV</td><td>Probably malignant</td><td>Require biopsy as prescribed</td></tr><tr><td>Class V</td><td>Possibly malignant</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cancer-detection-examinations">Cancer Detection Examinations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cancer-detection-examinations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-d14b55c2.jpeg" alt="img-41.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="biopsy">BIOPSY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#biopsy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>involves obtaining tissue samples by needle aspiration, or incision of tumor</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>NEEDLE BIOPSY</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>done by aspiration of tumor cells with needle and syringe</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>EXCISION BIOPSY</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>done by removing the entire tumor (small)</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>INCISION OR SUBTOTAL BIOPSY</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>done by taking only a part of the tumor (large)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cancer-detection-examinations">Cancer Detection Examinations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cancer-detection-examinations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="radiologic-examinations">RADIOLOGIC EXAMINATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#radiologic-examinations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>ultrasound (UTZ)</li>
<li>magnetic resonance imaging (MRI)</li>
<li>radiodiagnostic tests</li>
<li>computerized axial tomography (CT scan)</li>
<li>endoscopic examinations</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cancer-detection-examinations">Cancer Detection Examinations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cancer-detection-examinations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="laboratory-blood-tests">LABORATORY BLOOD TESTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#laboratory-blood-tests" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-hematologic-cbc">1. HEMATOLOGIC (CBC)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-hematologic-cbc" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>hemoglobin (hgb) and hematocrit (hct)
low in anemia, may indicate malignancy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>leukocytes (wbc)
immature WBCs high in leukemia, lymphomas
mature WBCs low in leukemia and metastatic dse
in bone marrow</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>platelets
high in chronic myelocytic leukemia (CML),
Hodgkins dse
low in acute lymphocytic leukemia (ALL), acute
myelocytic leukemia (AML), multiple
myeloma, bone marrow depression</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cancer-detection-examinations">Cancer Detection Examinations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cancer-detection-examinations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="laboratory-blood-tests">LABORATORY BLOOD TESTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#laboratory-blood-tests" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-tumor-markers">2. TUMOR MARKERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-tumor-markers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>alpha-feto-protein (AFP)
elevated in lung, testicular, pancreatic, colon, gastric CAs and choriocarcinoma</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>carcinoembryonic antigen (CEA)
elevated in colorectal, breast lung, stomach, pancreatic and prostate CAs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>human chorionic gonadotropin (HCG)
elevated in choriocarcinoma, germ cell, testicular CA</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>prostatic acid phosphatase
elevated in metastatic prostate CA</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>prostatic-specific antigen (PSA)
elevated in prostate CA</p>
</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cellular-abberations">CELLULAR ABBERATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cellular-abberations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cancer-cell-proliferation">CANCER CELL PROLIFERATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cancer-cell-proliferation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>disrupt normal cell growth and interfere with tissue function</li>
<li>Pressure</li>
<li>Obstruction</li>
<li>Pain</li>
<li>Effusion</li>
<li>Ulceration</li>
<li>Vascular thrombosis, thrombophlebitis</li>
</ul>
